<div id="review_2582939134" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2582939134" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2582939134?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2582939134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14545234780404728703">I'm about 3.5 stars here.<br/><br/>"When her children were small they'd sometimes say, 'What would you do if I died?' And she would reply, 'I would die too, because I could not live without you.' And then her child had died and she had found out that somehow, incredibly, she could live without her, that she had woken every morning for a hundred days, a thousand days, three thousand days and she had lived without her."<br/><br/>Ellie Mack was a golden child—beautiful, smart, popular. At 15, she was the apple of her </span>
  <span id="freeText14545234780404728703" style="display:none">I'm about 3.5 stars here.<br /><br />"When her children were small they'd sometimes say, 'What would you do if I died?' And she would reply, 'I would die too, because I could not live without you.' And then her child had died and she had found out that somehow, incredibly, she could live without her, that she had woken every morning for a hundred days, a thousand days, three thousand days and she had lived without her."<br /><br />Ellie Mack was a golden child—beautiful, smart, popular. At 15, she was the apple of her family's eye, well-liked by all, with a handsome boyfriend and a life full of possibility waiting for her. Then one day, Ellie was supposed to go to the library and be home by lunchtime, but she never made it there, and she never returned.<br /><br />For 10 years, Ellie's mother Laurel has held out a small sliver of hope that Ellie might have simply run away for some reason and she might come back, even though in her heart she knows her daughter is probably dead. This combination of despair and irrational hope has left Laurel's life a shambles, leading to the end of her marriage and straining her relationship with her two older children. <br /><br />But when a discovery helps provide some answers, Laurel decides it is time to get her life back. She meets a handsome man, Floyd Dunn, in a neighborhood cafe, and for the first time in 10 years, she realizes she can live for herself. She is surprised at how quickly she and Floyd fall for each other, and how quickly their connection deepens into a real relationship, and before she knows it, she is even meeting his daughters and spending weekends at his home.<br /><br />Laurel is immediately taken with Floyd's youngest daughter, Poppy, who is beautiful and wise beyond her years, truly an old soul. But Laurel cannot shake just how similar Poppy looks to Ellie, and how at times, when Poppy speaks, it is like she's in the same room with her daughter. As questions start to form in her mind about Floyd and what secrets he might be hiding, more and more her questions about Ellie's disappearance begin surfacing again. Did Ellie run away, or did she run into danger somehow? And why do Poppy and Ellie seem so similar?<br /><br />I'll admit, I figured out the plot of <b>
  <i>Then She Was Gone</i>
</b> fairly soon into the book. While it did detract a bit from my enjoyment of the book as the story continued to unfold, I was still captivated by the way Lisa Jewell teased out the suspense, making you wonder what surprises might pop up. Having never read any of Jewell's books before, I worried she might throw in some outrageous or melodramatic plot elements, and I was pleased that she didn't do that.<br /><br />Jewell is a terrific storyteller, and I raced through this entire book on a flight. While I certainly would have loved a little more surprise, I still thought this was a captivating and compelling read, and if you like thrillers, you may very well enjoy this one. <br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>, or check out my list of the best books I read in 2017 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2018/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2017.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2018/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2017.html</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14545234780404728703" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6594972588094327673" style="display:none">4 stars! This was a spine-tingling and addictive story!<br /><br />This novel follows Laurel whose teenage daughter, Ellie, went missing ten years ago. Laurel has been battling her grief since the day Ellie disappeared with the hope that she may one day come home. After Ellie’s disappearance, being swallowed up in her sadness and grief, Laurel’s marriage falls apart and she loses her connection with her two other children.<br /><br />The story is narrated by various characters in Laurel’s life through a Now and Then perspective, each character adding a new layer of suspense and appeal as the novel brilliantly unfolds.<br /><br />The author, Lisa Jewell, has a fantastic ability to pull you in right from the start. Her writing is strong, compelling and addictive. I look forward to reading more from her!<br /><br />This was a Traveling Sister read that we all enjoyed! To find this review, along with the other Traveling Sister reviews, please visit Brenda and Norma’s fabulous blog at:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com/2018/04/18/then-she-was-gone-by-lisa-jewell-lisajewelluk-atriabooks-simonschusterca-netgalley-bookreview-travelingsistersread/">https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com/2...</a><br /><br />A big thank you to NetGalley, Simon &amp; Schuster Canada and Lisa Jewell for providing me with an ARC in exchange for an honest review!!</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Theresa Alan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Theresa Alan" href="/user/show/3268839-theresa-alan">Theresa Alan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2352549769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4972183211428608826">This novel is creepy—in a good way. Fifteen-year-old Ellie disappears on her way to the library one day. Ultimately, since police can’t find anything, they suspect she’s a runaway despite the fact she had a boyfriend she loved and was looking forward to taking the exams she’d been studying hard for.<br/><br/>When we meet up with her mother Laurel ten years later, Laurel’s relationships with her other daughter, her son, and her now-ex-husband have all suffered greatly because they’d never found a body or a</span>
  <span id="freeText4972183211428608826" style="display:none">This novel is creepy—in a good way. Fifteen-year-old Ellie disappears on her way to the library one day. Ultimately, since police can’t find anything, they suspect she’s a runaway despite the fact she had a boyfriend she loved and was looking forward to taking the exams she’d been studying hard for.<br /><br />When we meet up with her mother Laurel ten years later, Laurel’s relationships with her other daughter, her son, and her now-ex-husband have all suffered greatly because they’d never found a body or any evidence of where Ellie may have gone. The not knowing if Ellie is alive or dead has made it impossible for Laurel to move on.<br /><br />New evidence comes to light at the same time Laurel falls for Floyd, her first relationship with a man since she and her husband separated seven years earlier. At first, the romance is dizzyingly exciting. Then, certain things that Lloyd does start to niggle at Laurel. Something doesn’t seem quite right.<br /><br />This was not my favorite suspense novel that I’ve read recently, so if you’re strapped for time, I might go with another book. It’s good, but not great, in part because you can guess at a huge part of the mystery (and be right) well before everything is revealed. <br /><br />Thanks to NetGalley for the opportunity to review this mystery, which will be published in the States on April 17, 2018. <br /><br />For more reviews, please visit: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.theresaalan.net/blog">http://www.theresaalan.net/blog</a><br /></span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2600604242?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/4125660-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4125660-liz?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2600604242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15308224261492772861"><br/>Maybe I’m getting bored by psychological thrillers. Maybe the narrator’s voice just irritated me, especially when she was channeling Poppy’s voice or when her attempt at Floyd’s voice changed with each chapter. Or maybe I could see where it was going way too early in the book. Or maybe I’m just jaundiced by the idea of a perfect man showing up at the table next to an older divorced woman. Regardless, I wasn’t as enthralled with this one as the majority. Don’t get me wrong, it was okay. I just di</span>
  <span id="freeText15308224261492772861" style="display:none"><br />Maybe I’m getting bored by psychological thrillers. Maybe the narrator’s voice just irritated me, especially when she was channeling Poppy’s voice or when her attempt at Floyd’s voice changed with each chapter. Or maybe I could see where it was going way too early in the book. Or maybe I’m just jaundiced by the idea of a perfect man showing up at the table next to an older divorced woman. Regardless, I wasn’t as enthralled with this one as the majority. Don’t get me wrong, it was okay. I just didn’t love it. I think this is one of those books that I had such high hopes for that I let myself expect too much. <br /><br />The book lacks any real sense of suspense. The big secrets were pretty obvious and it soon became only a question of how the characters would figure it out. <br /><br />I enjoyed Watching You so I will definitely give Jewell another chance. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15308224261492772861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2384859088" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2384859088" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9472704-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336837712p2/9472704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2384859088?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/9472704-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/34806691-then-she-was-gone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=mystery-thrillers">mystery-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2384859088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6354272202795552920">"People try and make out there's a greater purpose, a secret meaning, that it all means something. And it doesn't."<br/><br/>Loss is like that. There's no justifying it. There are no words of wisdom that can ever buffer the pain. It becomes a life sentence worn like the weight of a sack cloth far into eternity and beyond.<br/><br/>Laurel Mack is a grieving mother. Period. Her beautiful daughter, Ellie, disappeared one day on her way to her weekly lesson with her math tutor. There is no evidence, no clues, no remnan</span>
  <span id="freeText6354272202795552920" style="display:none">"People try and make out there's a greater purpose, a secret meaning, that it all means something. And it doesn't."<br /><br />Loss is like that. There's no justifying it. There are no words of wisdom that can ever buffer the pain. It becomes a life sentence worn like the weight of a sack cloth far into eternity and beyond.<br /><br />Laurel Mack is a grieving mother. Period. Her beautiful daughter, Ellie, disappeared one day on her way to her weekly lesson with her math tutor. There is no evidence, no clues, no remnants of a missing Ellie even after ten years. The police have leaned toward labeling this case as a teenage runaway. Nothing could be farther than the truth in Laurel's eyes.<br /><br />As time passes, the deep love imprint of the missing Ellie has left its mark on the Mack family. Laurel and her husband, Paul, have divorced. Grief sometimes forces a wedge between individuals who are saturated in its unspeakable sorrow. Their now adult children, Jake and Hanna, have carved out separate lives that interact briefly with their parents now and then. Different directions with different intentions.<br /><br />But Laurel has met an attractive man in a coffee shop that she frequents. She and Floyd seem to hit it off well with unexpected humor as the draw. Floyd has two daughters: the more serious Sarah Jade and the vivacious young Poppy. But it is Poppy with her rich brown hair and strategic dimple that makes Laurel do a double take. She envisions her lost Ellie in the persona of Poppy. Coincidence or merely a longing of the soul?<br /><br />Lisa Jewell presents a storyline that begins with the tragedy of a missing daughter and a family's downward spiral in its aftermath. But she doesn't allow you to sit with this reality too long in your lap. The chapters will occasionally revert from the present to "Then" as the rough edges of Ellie's story come to light. There will also be moments of celebration as Laurel slowly removes layer upon layer of her self-imposed isolation and begins a life with Floyd.<br /><br />As readers, we will note that Lisa Jewell tends to stretch the borders of reality in some scenes. But the main thread is captivating and it tugs at us to delve deeper into this story. As in a fine-tuned musical piece, there will be quite the crescendo at the end even though you may have a sense of where all this is leading. High interest, unusual characters, breadcrumbs into the fire will all make this a must read when you long for something to take you out of the doldrums. Looking forward to more from this author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6354272202795552920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Dem" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dem" href="/user/show/2752994-dem">Dem</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2752994-dem?shelf=psychological-thrillers">psychological-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2752994-dem?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2538443780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer893088978575689555"><b>Oh! I did love this clever and compelling, taut psychological thriller which kept me up until the wee hours the morning. My fist Lisa Jewell novel and lucky me as she appears to have a list of thrillers which I cant wait to try.</b><br/><br/>I listened to this one on audible and it was just so well narrated, the voice of Noelle Donnelly was just so perfect and she sent shivers down my spine. Well paced and not too dramatic this just works beautifully on audible.<br/><br/>Jewell writes wonderfully engaging characters, f</span>
  <span id="freeText893088978575689555" style="display:none"><b>Oh! I did love this clever and compelling, taut psychological thriller which kept me up until the wee hours the morning. My fist Lisa Jewell novel and lucky me as she appears to have a list of thrillers which I cant wait to try.</b><br /><br />I listened to this one on audible and it was just so well narrated, the voice of Noelle Donnelly was just so perfect and she sent shivers down my spine. Well paced and not too dramatic this just works beautifully on audible.<br /><br />Jewell writes wonderfully engaging characters, fresh and vivid, but quite believable. I actually had images of the characters in my head from the first few chapters and I think this is one of those rare psychological thrillers when asked in a years time for the synopsis I will be able to remember it clearly from all the other thrillers I have read and for me this is the rare and a real winner.<br />The plot is suspenseful, fast paced and lots of twists and turns to keep the reader turning those pages. I had guessed mid way through where this was going but it didn't take away from the unravelling of the story in any way and there was a little suspending of disbelief along the way but hey! its a novel and its supposed to take us out of the real world for a little while.<br /><br /><b>Chilling, Disturbing and gripping are three words to describe this one and I hope my Goodreads friend’s will recommend more by this author for me to devour.</b></span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2604913165?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandice" href="/user/show/36348070-brandice">Brandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2604913165" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3188613904806990842"><i>Then She Was Gone</i> was my first Lisa Jewell read and it won’t be my last! I was intrigued right from the start. <br/><br/>15 year old Ellie Mack leaves home to study one day and never returns. Understandably, her disappearance alters the life of her mother, Laurel. She has changed with the loss of her daughter. Distance builds between her and her other two children, Hannah and Jake. Her marriage to Paul also falls apart. Years later, Laurel meets an attractive man, Floyd, and begins a relationship with him</span>
  <span id="freeText3188613904806990842" style="display:none"><i>Then She Was Gone</i> was my first Lisa Jewell read and it won’t be my last! I was intrigued right from the start. <br /><br />15 year old Ellie Mack leaves home to study one day and never returns. Understandably, her disappearance alters the life of her mother, Laurel. She has changed with the loss of her daughter. Distance builds between her and her other two children, Hannah and Jake. Her marriage to Paul also falls apart. Years later, Laurel meets an attractive man, Floyd, and begins a relationship with him. He has a 9 year old daughter, Poppy, who bears a striking resemblance to Ellie. What is going on here?! <br /><br />I listened to the audiobook, narrated by Helen Duff. I enjoyed it a lot and she was a great narrator, reading with enthusiasm as well as distinction between voices of the different characters, as the story is told through multiple POVs.<br /><br /><i>Then She Was Gone</i> is a suspenseful read that both mystery novices and pros will likely enjoy. It’s a dark story, and even when the big picture of <i>what</i> was going on became clear, I was still interested and had to know the <i>why</i> and the <i>how</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3188613904806990842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2371365232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13468150850999157930">Then She Was Gone is a very mild title compared to the volcanic torment and angst behind the cover. Teenage daughter Ellie goes missing and blah blah blah...except that it's not so clear cut or cliched.<br/><br/>The action takes place in multiple points of view, and it's a treat to be fed factoid after factoid to try and make sense. It's deliciously excruciating how the info builds up to shape up the final solution.<br/><br/>Lisa Jewell is part of the latest generation of writers. The latter have bypassed Chaucer, </span>
  <span id="freeText13468150850999157930" style="display:none">Then She Was Gone is a very mild title compared to the volcanic torment and angst behind the cover. Teenage daughter Ellie goes missing and blah blah blah...except that it's not so clear cut or cliched.<br /><br />The action takes place in multiple points of view, and it's a treat to be fed factoid after factoid to try and make sense. It's deliciously excruciating how the info builds up to shape up the final solution.<br /><br />Lisa Jewell is part of the latest generation of writers. The latter have bypassed Chaucer, Milton, and Shakespeare to shape up to be gifted writers. Lisa Jewell is part of this disconnected generation. This was a wonderful book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13468150850999157930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2355179692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17608942701658716320">Traveling Sisters group read that we all enjoyed and it lead to a great discussion amongst us. <br/><br/>We all were immediately drawn into this intriguing story right from start to the rewarding and very satisfying ending that we all loved. <br/><br/>Lisa Jewell brilliantly creates a well-written and perfectly paced story to create a good, intriguing suspenseful story. Just at the right time, she reveals enough of the story to create suspense and then gives us understanding and insight into her characters rather t</span>
  <span id="freeText17608942701658716320" style="display:none">Traveling Sisters group read that we all enjoyed and it lead to a great discussion amongst us. <br /><br />We all were immediately drawn into this intriguing story right from start to the rewarding and very satisfying ending that we all loved. <br /><br />Lisa Jewell brilliantly creates a well-written and perfectly paced story to create a good, intriguing suspenseful story. Just at the right time, she reveals enough of the story to create suspense and then gives us understanding and insight into her characters rather than creating a shocking twisty story. She balances the darkest well by adding just the right amount of disturbing and creepy along with the insight into the well-developed characters’ emotions, creating emotional layers to the characters along with layers to the plot.<br /><br />Some of us have read a few of Lisa Jewell's books and loved them all and the rest of us will be looking into reading more of her books. For me, I have read a few and have a couple to review. <br />I highly recommend Then She Was Gone.<br /><br /><br />Thank you, NetGalley, Atria Books, and Lisa Jewell for a copy to read and review. <br />for more Traveling Sister reviews <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://travelingsistersbookreviews.com">https://travelingsistersbookreviews.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17608942701658716320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RIaXSQE8/1OFbaLQIqd0c/IviCsVq8B4T3W8l/vMN9EfcV/hPVc11ZB7DzwrSyPMSFQqMe8NMvTLt96lMaXanQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3VR3+nFq9CLe/bdY5bAiCmZKHbmEPIvPLlP+JO+U3FqGo79STQE+pMvrGrTsXHW13DG/o36aeUOqkZwWJf0xFg==')})
  }

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_40097951'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40097951-the-silent-patient?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Silent Patient<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/17621440.Alex_Michaelides?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Alex Michaelides<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.09 avg rating &mdash; 527,675 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2019\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer9791318229877699394\">The Silent Patient is a shocking psychological thriller of a woman’s act of violence against her husband—and of the therapist obsessed with uncovering her motive.\n\nAlicia Berenson’s life is seemingly perfect. A famous painter married to an in-demand <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText9791318229877699394\" style=\"display:none\">The Silent Patient is a shocking psychological thriller of a woman’s act of violence against her husband—and of the therapist obsessed with uncovering her motive.\n\nAlicia Berenson’s life is seemingly perfect. A famous painter married to an in-demand fashion photographer, she lives in a grand house with big windows overlooking a park in one of London’s most desirable areas. One evening her husband Gabriel returns home late from a fashion shoot, and Alicia shoots him five times in the face, and then never speaks another word.\n\nAlicia’s refusal to talk, or give any kind of explanation, turns a domestic tragedy into something far grander, a mystery that captures the public imagination and casts Alicia into notoriety. The price of her art skyrockets, and she, the silent patient, is hidden away from the tabloids and spotlight at the Grove, a secure forensic unit in North London.\n\nTheo Faber is a criminal psychotherapist who has waited a long time for the opportunity to work with Alicia.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/93504.Lisa_Jewell">About Lisa Jewell</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5869953815137542715">Lisa was born in London in 1968. Her mother was a secretary and her father was a textile agent and she was brought up in the northernmost reaches of London with her two younger sisters. She was educated at a Catholic girls’ Grammar school in Finchley. After leaving school at sixteen she spent two years at Barnet College doing an arts foundation course and then two years at Epsom School of Art & De</span>
  <span id="freeText5869953815137542715" style="display:none">Lisa was born in London in 1968. Her mother was a secretary and her father was a textile agent and she was brought up in the northernmost reaches of London with her two younger sisters. She was educated at a Catholic girls’ Grammar school in Finchley. After leaving school at sixteen she spent two years at Barnet College doing an arts foundation course and then two years at Epsom School of Art &amp; Design studying Fashion Illustration and Communication.<br /><br />She worked for the fashion chain Warehouse for three years as a PR assistant and then for Thomas Pink, the Jermyn Street shirt company for four years as a receptionist and PA. She started her first novel, Ralph’s Party, for a bet in 1996. She finished it in 1997 and it was published by Penguin books in May 1998. It went on to become the best-selling debut novel of that year.<br /><br />She has since written a further nine novels, as is currently at work on her eleventh.<br /><br />She now lives in an innermost part of north London with her husband Jascha, an IT consultant, her daughters, Amelie and Evie and her silver tabbies, Jack and Milly.<br /><br /><br />Lisa's Facebook page:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/LisaJewellofficial">http://www.facebook.com/LisaJewelloff...</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5869953815137542715" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
